## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the central problem in mathematical population ecology. Classical models range from simple exponential growth to density-dependent and time-varying models.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential (Malthusian) growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (unlimited growth, no density dependence)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / (P + 1e-10)) (asymmetric sigmoidal growth, common in tumor/biological growth)
- Theta-logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P * c1 - 1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth fails below critical population threshold)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P ** c1 - c2 * P (anabolic vs catabolic scaling)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P) ** c2) * c3 (generalized asymmetric growth curve)
- Logistic with harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (constant yield harvesting)
- Time-dependent Malthusian: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (exponentially changing growth rate)
- Logistic with time-varying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * exp(c2 * t)) (carrying capacity changes over time)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P ** c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (ratio-dependent growth minus mortality)
- Periodic forcing: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t)) (seasonal variation in growth)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P ** 2 + c2 * P ** 3 (higher-order density effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Linear dependence on P (dP_dt proportional to P) → exponential/Malthusian regime indicating no density feedback
- Product of P with (1 - P/K) structure → logistic-type density regulation with a stable equilibrium at carrying capacity
- Logarithmic terms log(K/P) multiplied by P → Gompertz-type growth with slower approach to carrying capacity from above vs below
- Cubic or triple-root structure in P (three zeros) → Allee effect with both extinction and carrying capacity equilibria
- Difference of power laws (P^a - P^b) → competing metabolic scaling processes (anabolism vs catabolism)
- Sinusoidal dependence on t → seasonal or periodic environmental forcing on growth parameters
- Exponential dependence on t multiplied by population terms → non-stationary environment with trend in resources or conditions
- Rational function of P (P/(1+cP)) → saturating per-capita growth rate due to resource competition or interference
- Sign change in dP_dt at intermediate P values → bistability or Allee threshold requiring minimum viable population
- Independence from t (dP_dt depends only on P) → autonomous system suggesting stable environmental conditions

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG7)
============================================================
GT: c0*(-c1 + P/c2)*(c3 - P/c4)*P + c5*(c6 - P/c7)*P + c8*P**c9
Candidate formulas: 65

I need to simplify the GT expression first.

**GT numerical expression:**
`0.7213553457664288*(-1 + P/6.6511035054181695)*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*(1 - P/13.538092585698905)*P + 0.7213553457664288*P**0.333333333333333`

Let me denote α = 0.72136, a = 6.6511, b = 13.538.

First term: α*(-1 + P/a)*(1 - P/b)*P
Second term: α*(1 - P/b)*P
Third term: α*P^(1/3)

Combine first and second terms - they share the factor α*(1 - P/b)*P:
α*(1 - P/b)*P * [(-1 + P/a) + 1] = α*(1 - P/b)*P * (P/a)
= α*(P²/a)*(1 - P/b)
= α*P²/a - α*P³/(a*b)

So the GT simplifies to:
**α*P^(1/3) + (α/a)*P² - (α/(a*b))*P³**

Computing constants:
- α/a = 0.72136/6.6511 ≈ 0.10846
- α/(a*b) = 0.72136/(6.6511 × 13.538) ≈ 0.008009

So GT = **0.72136·P^(1/3) + 0.10846·P² - 0.008009·P³**

This is of the form: **c₀·P^(1/3) + c₁·P³ + c₂·P²**

Now checking candidate 43: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P**3*c1 + P**2*c2`

This is exactly: c0·P^(1/3) + c1·P³ + c2·P²

Setting:
- c0 = 0.72136
- c1 = -0.008009
- c2 = 0.10846

This matches the GT perfectly!

Let me verify by re-expanding the GT more carefully:

First term: α*(-1 + P/a)*(1 - P/b)*P
= α*P*[(-1)(1 - P/b) + (P/a)(1 - P/b)]
= α*P*[-1 + P/b + P/a - P²/(ab)]
= α*[-P + P²/b + P²/a - P³/(ab)]

Second term: α*(1 - P/b)*P = α*[P - P²/b]

Adding first + second:
α*[-P + P²/b + P²/a - P³/(ab) + P - P²/b]
= α*[P²/a - P³/(ab)]

Third term: α*P^(1/3)

Total: α*P^(1/3) + α*P²/a - α*P³/(ab) ✓

This confirms the GT = c0·P^(1/3) + c2·P² + c1·P³, which matches candidate 43.

Also checking candidate 44: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P**3*c1 + P**2*c2 + P**2*c3` - this works too (with c3=0), but candidate 43 is the exact match.

And candidate 32: `P**(1/3)*c0 + P**3*c1 + P**2*c2 + P*c3` - works with c3=0.

Many candidates with extra terms that can be zeroed out would work, but the cleanest match is candidate 43.

[MATCH FOUND]

Candidate **43** (`P**(1/3)*c0 + P**3*c1 + P**2*c2`) is mathematically equivalent to the GT with:
- c0 = 0.72136
- c1 = -0.008009
- c2 = 0.10846

The GT simplifies because the first two terms combine: α*(-1+P/a)*(1-P/b)*P + α*(1-P/b)*P = α*(P/a)*(1-P/b)*P = (α/a)*P² - (α/(ab))*P³, yielding exactly the form P^(1/3)·c0 + P³·c1 + P²·c2.

Additionally, many other candidates (e.g., 32, 28, 31, 36, 39, 44, etc.) can also match by setting their extra parameters to zero.

Conclusion: Match found

I need to first simplify the Ground Truth expression to understand its structure.

**GT expression:**
$$0.7214(-1 + P/6.651)(1 - P/13.538)P + 0.7214(1 - P/13.538)P + 0.7214 P^{1/3}$$

Let me expand this. Let me denote $a = 0.7214$, $b = 6.651$, $d = 13.538$.

First term: $a(-1 + P/b)(1 - P/d)P$
$= a(P/b - 1)(1 - P/d)P$
$= a(P/b - P^2/(bd) - 1 + P/d)P$
$= a(P^2/b - P^3/(bd) - P + P^2/d)$

Second term: $a(1 - P/d)P = a(P - P^2/d)$

Third term: $aP^{1/3}$

Combining all:
- $P^3$: $-a/(bd) = -0.7214/(6.651 \times 13.538) \approx -0.7214/90.07 \approx -0.008010$
- $P^2$: $a/b + a/d - a/d = a/b \approx 0.7214/6.651 \approx 0.10846$
- $P$: $-a + a = 0$
- $P^{1/3}$: $a \approx 0.7214$

So the GT simplifies to:
$$GT = c_a P^{1/3} + c_b P^3 + c_c P^2$$

where $c_a = 0.7214$, $c_b = -a/(bd)$, $c_c = a/b$.

**This is exactly: $\alpha P^{1/3} + \beta P^3 + \gamma P^2$**

Now let me check which candidates can match this form (with free constants).

The GT has the form: $c_0 P^{1/3} + c_1 P^3 + c_2 P^2$ with specific constants.
